        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139666822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer879084569868974793">I am one of the luckiest Goodreaders who actually won a copy of this book via the Goodreads Firstreads Giveaways. When I received the news I was really happy, happy because I think this was the very first time I actually won something through luck.<br/><br/>I actually have no idea who the author was and what was the book was all about because I just randomly enter any books that are listed in the Giveaway list. So I'm like Sandra Brown Who? Nevertheless someone commented that Sandra Brown was a good autho</span>
  <span id="freeText879084569868974793" style="display:none">I am one of the luckiest Goodreaders who actually won a copy of this book via the Goodreads Firstreads Giveaways. When I received the news I was really happy, happy because I think this was the very first time I actually won something through luck.<br /><br />I actually have no idea who the author was and what was the book was all about because I just randomly enter any books that are listed in the Giveaway list. So I'm like Sandra Brown Who? Nevertheless someone commented that Sandra Brown was a good author so even though I have no idea if I'll like the book or not I'm still excited to read it.<br /><br />The book actually arrived very late and it just arrived this month of July when supposedly it should arrived earlier like in the months of January or February.My mom was the one who received the package and she was very delightful when she learned that I just got that free from a giveaway contest. <br /><br />The package contained the book Envy, the one I won and another book which is called Chill Factor. The book Envy was in hardbound and I'm really glad because it was actually signed by the author. Which for me was also a first time to have a book that was actually have the author's signature in it.<br /><br />I am really anxious to read it and I don't know what to expect. I was pleased that from the very first chapter I got hooked and I simply can't stop reading. The one thing I really liked about it was that you'll learn a lot of things about writing a novel, publishing, books, authors etc. I do like that this book draw me to that experience wherein I learned so much about book business because you know I really like books and it's just really interesting to know more about how novels are made.<br /><br />I really like the concept of this one, there are two stories involved in this book, the story itself and also the story about Envy, the novel that this mysterious writer was trying to write. It's like there's a story and then within it there's another story. The plot of this book is layered between the two stories.<br /><br />I could have given these 5 stars, it was a good story actually, it will keep you guessing and you'll find yourself reading and turning pages and after the end of a chapter you'll get more excited to get into another chapter. However I was disappointed on how everything ended I just felt that the mystery of the novel was really strong at the beginning but at the end it was just okay how the mysteries were revealed one by one and honestly I didn't feel that much excitement.<br /><br />I really recommend it if you like romance and suspense in a novel and I just want to say that I really like this more rather than The Women's Murder Club and The Girl With The Dragon Tattoo. </span>

<div id="review_1809920" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809920" />
    <a title="Sarah Sammis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122647-sarah-sammis"><img alt="Sarah Sammis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181271036p2/122647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809920?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Sammis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Sammis" href="/user/show/122647-sarah-sammis">Sarah Sammis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=released">released</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=read-in-2007">read-in-2007</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15389185420956000972">Envy is the third novel by Sandra Brown I've read and she's rapidly earning her way onto my list of "go-to" authors. Her novels always manage to surprise once or twice and certainly entertain from cover to cover.<br/><br/>Envy is the title of the book within the book and it's the lure that brings Maris Matherly-Reed to a remote Georgian island to purchase the rights to a novel. What she doesn't realize is that she's been lured into an elaborate scheme of revenge long buried in the past.<br/><br/>There are excerpts </span>
  <span id="freeText15389185420956000972" style="display:none">Envy is the third novel by Sandra Brown I've read and she's rapidly earning her way onto my list of "go-to" authors. Her novels always manage to surprise once or twice and certainly entertain from cover to cover.<br /><br />Envy is the title of the book within the book and it's the lure that brings Maris Matherly-Reed to a remote Georgian island to purchase the rights to a novel. What she doesn't realize is that she's been lured into an elaborate scheme of revenge long buried in the past.<br /><br />There are excerpts of the fictional Envy included as interludes between some of the more emotionally charged chapters. They are there both as background information and as a character building device to better understand Parker, the author Maris has gone to see. Frankly, these chapters aren't necessary and serve as a distraction to the meat of the book. I suggest saving them until the end to read as bonus material.<br /><br />Envy has three major story lines: Parker's past, the romance between Parker and Maris, and Noah's machinations to sell Maris's publishing company out from under her. Noah Reed, Maris's husband and her relationship to him is the glue that holds Envy together.<br /><br />What I liked best about the novel was Parker. He's wheelchair bound but by no means "handicapped" nor is he seeking sympathy or special treatment. He's rough, crude and fowl mouthed and tempered and yet he's a very believable and oddly likeable character. It's clear that the wheelchair isn't the cause of his "bad" traits; it's just another part of who he is. It was refreshing to meet characters like Parker who weren't obviously built up from a series of checked boxes on a character sheet. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15389185420956000972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer695608343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8983149115654733529"><s> Note to myself: need to re-read this one. I remember that I loved it back in 2013, and I think I liked the story, the mystery more than the romance itself </s><br/><br/><b> 4.5 stars </b><br/><br/>I read this book back in 2013 and it was my favourite Sandra Brown book.<br/><br/>So I was very excited to re-read it and see if my opinions have changed. Actually, I was so excited that every time that I read a sentence in prologue I would log out of my kindle and go click some youtube video. I was just so giddy and couldn’t concentrate lol</span>
  <span id="freeText8983149115654733529" style="display:none"><s> Note to myself: need to re-read this one. I remember that I loved it back in 2013, and I think I liked the story, the mystery more than the romance itself </s><br><br><b> 4.5 stars </b><br><br>I read this book back in 2013 and it was my favourite Sandra Brown book.<br><br>So I was very excited to re-read it and see if my opinions have changed. Actually, I was so excited that every time that I read a sentence in prologue I would log out of my kindle and go click some youtube video. I was just so giddy and couldn’t concentrate lol does anybody else do this?<br><br>However, once again I enjoyed this book and it is still one my favourite from SB.<br>To me, the prologue is one of the best I have read. It pulls you in, giving you just hints and you are left confused and wanting for more.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471024662ra/19993490.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I won’t be writing about plot, actually I won’t be writing much at all. Why? Because it’s best to go blind into this book. Seriously, I would advise not reading synopsis either.<br><br>And for all those people who like looking for, reading, investigating for spoilers:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471024662ra/19993491.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, that was a bit harsh Benedict. But you got my point.<br><br>Do you enjoy mystery? Suspense? Good book atmosphere? If your answers are ‘yes’ then this book is for you.<br><br>I really enjoyed this book, and although there are some times when it’s tiny bit predictable, and some characters are one dimensional, this book had that atmosphere that only some authors can create. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471024662ra/19993492.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I was thoroughly enjoying it. I couldn’t put it down, and I think my feelings changed every second.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471024662ra/19993493.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wanted to punch some characters, including the heroine sometimes<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471024662ra/19993494.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I admit, some chapters were a bit predictable<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=29blzr4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471024662ra/19993495.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But overall it was enjoyable and interesting<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471024662ra/19993496.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My two main problems were: sometimes the heroine was too naive, I won’t reveal why but whoever read it will know. I know that she is this romantic at heart character, but some of her doings were a little too naive for me. I just wanted to yell at her<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471024662i/19993497._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And the other is, I would have liked an epilogue, few years later with them and I wouldn't mind babies and whole cheesy hea thing lol. To me their reunion was kinda glossed over, and I wanted more grovelling although he did explain, but I just wanted my dose of romance.<br><br>It’s more a mystery than a romance to me, but it was all nicely packaged.<br><br>It wasn’t perfect that’s for sure, some characters could benefit from better development, and some scenes could be better, but it just all clicked to me, I got lost in that atmosphere, and I really envy (pun intended) to anyone who is reading it for the first time. But again please don’t read spoilers or plenty of reviews or anything just decide if you want to read this kind of book and go for it, you can do it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471024662i/19993498.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer176170036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer686314198820763988">Just started the audiobook on a trip and was so mesmerized, I didn't want the trip to end. <br/><br/>UPDATE: <br/><br/>WOW!!!! I have to say, I loved this book! Just wow. Way to go Ms. Brown!<br/>~D~</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136585966?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taryn" href="/user/show/13977687-taryn">Taryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136585966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5814789873077464148">This book is pretty fun but also hasn’t aged super well, like Chumbawamba’s “Tubthumping” and a lot of other things from the ‘90s. There’s no doubt Sandra Brown can spin a good yarn, and I especially enjoyed this one in audio, thanks to the silky southern drawl of Parker, the mysterious and reclusive author at the center of the mystery. I couldn’t have guessed all the twists and turns, and one particular detail of the ending genuinely surprised me. But there’s some unfortunate racism, misogyny, </span>
  <span id="freeText5814789873077464148" style="display:none">This book is pretty fun but also hasn’t aged super well, like Chumbawamba’s “Tubthumping” and a lot of other things from the ‘90s. There’s no doubt Sandra Brown can spin a good yarn, and I especially enjoyed this one in audio, thanks to the silky southern drawl of Parker, the mysterious and reclusive author at the center of the mystery. I couldn’t have guessed all the twists and turns, and one particular detail of the ending genuinely surprised me. But there’s some unfortunate racism, misogyny, homophobia, and fat-shaming that struck my ear really wrong, and I would be remiss not to mention it. I would like to think that most of it wouldn’t make it past an editor in 2017. It’s a shame, because it mars what otherwise is a fun, fluffy, sexy thriller with a teeth-grindingly terrible villain who deserves every bit of what’s coming to him.<br /><br />More book recommendations by me at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readingwithhippos.com">www.readingwithhippos.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5814789873077464148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_289622651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/289622651" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2038521-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365440426p2/2038521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289622651?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/2038521-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780446611800" href="/book/show/790250.Envy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2038521-anna?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289622651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13142651314415858194">It shouldn't come as much of a surprise that with a plot like <i>Envy</i>'s, there's a big emphasis on writerly things, and nearly all of the characters are involved in the industry at some point, either from the writing or the publishing aspect. Ironically, the criticism given to one of her writing characters pretty much sums up the book: lively dialogue, but the plot needs work. The plot needs a lot of work, because I don't have enough suspension of disbelief to buy the story past the first fifty pag</span>
  <span id="freeText13142651314415858194" style="display:none">It shouldn't come as much of a surprise that with a plot like <i>Envy</i>'s, there's a big emphasis on writerly things, and nearly all of the characters are involved in the industry at some point, either from the writing or the publishing aspect. Ironically, the criticism given to one of her writing characters pretty much sums up the book: lively dialogue, but the plot needs work. The plot needs a lot of work, because I don't have enough suspension of disbelief to buy the story past the first fifty pages. A successful and extremely busy New York publisher is going to drop everything to hunt down an author who didn't bother to leave contact information? Not only that, but she's going to fund a trip to visit him when he rudely informs her over the phone he's not interested in pursuing publication? Let's not even get into how she agrees to pay him when he tells her the manuscript hasn't been written past the first chapter, because that chapter made my head hurt (ok, the headache might have had to do with the way I wound up pounding my head against the wall). How a book that understands the role of publishers so little ever got published, I will never understand.<br /><br />Every character in this book is two-dimensional. The villain has no redeeming qualities, so everything he does, thinks, or says is malicious or evil in some way. Maris's father is meant to be shrewd, so he winds up being omnipotent and able to predict everyone's actions, although he doesn't often do anything with that knowledge. Maris herself is a big plot device. Her personality shifts as needed to carry on the plot, which often makes her dumber than dirt. Really dumb dirt, at that. "I have caught this person involved in my personal and professional life, who happens to be in a key position of my family company, in some nefarious activities and have reason to believe he is thoroughly villainous, but I am just going to sit on that information rather than actually doing something about it. I should probably tell my father, and the head of the company, what is going on but I won't because that would not only be logical, it would take a good 100 pages or so out of the book." What makes this even better is that everyone throughout the book refers to Maris as being very smart, which would normally make me grit my teeth except that I started reading it as though they were all patronizing her, which made me laugh.<br /><br />Ok, the characterization and plot need work, but it's not all bad. The prose itself is very readable, and the dialogue is good (when it's not revealing the flat characters). It's the kind of writing where although nothing in the book makes sense, it's at least not painful to do the actual reading. The book is trying too hard (and failing) to be a mystery, and although the tone is about right, there's a lack of actual mystery, which you'd think would be one of the given elements, but apparently not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13142651314415858194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_430526077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430526077" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7451210-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434101513p2/7451210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430526077?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/7451210-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=absolute-favourite">absolute-favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=handicap-scarred-hero">handicap-scarred-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430526077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16002525685072967112">I remember reading this sometime ago, the mystery really drew me in. I would say this is one of the romantic suspense with the strongest plot I ever read. From the start, we are wondering what is Parker's motivation, why is he handicap and what is the connection between the current events and the story of Envy.<br/><br/>Parker is a recluse living in an island and he is also novelist who happen to send in the initially chapter of his novel titled 'Envy' to Maris' publishing company. Maris is the owner of t</span>
  <span id="freeText16002525685072967112" style="display:none">I remember reading this sometime ago, the mystery really drew me in. I would say this is one of the romantic suspense with the strongest plot I ever read. From the start, we are wondering what is Parker's motivation, why is he handicap and what is the connection between the current events and the story of Envy.<br /><br />Parker is a recluse living in an island and he is also novelist who happen to send in the initially chapter of his novel titled 'Envy' to Maris' publishing company. Maris is the owner of the company and also an editor, she was fascinated with the story and the author himself. She decided to seek him out and negotiate a contract with him and hope he can finish the story soon. <br /><br />The current story with Maris and Parker was woven together with some of the chapters from Envy itself. Envy is a story about two college friends who studied English literature together. They are best friends and they are also rivals. From the beginning, I can't wait to see how both story will actually merge together in the end.<br /><br />There is really no way to talk about the plot without giving out some spoiler. I will just said that for those who loves reading romantic suspense with a great mystery, this is highly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16002525685072967112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3565377751" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3565377751" />
    <a title="ȷαεlα" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16126654-l"><img alt="ȷαεlα" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589706072p2/16126654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3565377751?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ȷαεlα" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ȷαεlα" href="/user/show/16126654-l">ȷαεlα</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3565377751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5548089479792591696">I think this is SB’s best book. Usually I don’t like to read when there’s a story within a story, but here it was beautifully executed, and I was looking forward to “the story”.<br/>I wouldn’t call this a thriller, nonetheless there was too much suspense.<br/>And the villain? Omg I just wanted to strangle him! If you can make the readers hate a character, then you’ve succeeded in portraying him.<br/>Wow</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('reSbsDR5SBXWMB80DkBm+RAPO6QHObWADUKA8Iy1nvzOmz9qAiisIukVv2RZak4Ln69OCqXIrLL88q0wyOfrmQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ynQp8k4g4JMnDqArr1tMZB9Tv/qd/syPuv8qg+M1KpSpC40oeHEEpBgrAHv4cWSWkPPKVD8P1b1LTwdDp2df8Q==')})
  }

Preacher’s kids, Hal has taken the righteous path, while Cage is the unrepentant black sheep of the family. The only thing they have in common is their love for the same woman – Jenny Fletcher. Jenny loves Hal for his commitment to his calling, but deep in her heart of hearts she wishes his desire for her burned as hotly. Only on the eve of his departure for a dangerous mission trip to Central America, when he comes to her bed in darkness and secret, does he take her with unexpected passion.  When tragedy strikes and Hal is lost to her, it’s that night that Jenny cherishes, that Hal she misses. She yearns for that lover whose unbridled sensuality more resembled. . . Cage.  For Jenny, Cage is willing to give up his wild ways. <span id="freeTextContainer16709448667899162189"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a> </i> <br/><br/>Sandra Brown is the author of more than sixty New York Times bestsellers, including STING (2016), FRICTION (2015), MEAN STREAK (2014), DEADLINE(2013), & LOW PRESSURE (2012), LETHAL (2011).<br/><br/>Brown began her writing career in 1981 and since then has published over seventy nove</span>
  <span id="freeText16709448667899162189" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a> </i> <br /><br />Sandra Brown is the author of more than sixty New York Times bestsellers, including STING (2016), FRICTION (2015), MEAN STREAK (2014), DEADLINE(2013), &amp; LOW PRESSURE (2012), LETHAL (2011).<br /><br />Brown began her writing career in 1981 and since then has published over seventy novels, bringing the number of copies of her books in print worldwide to upwards of eighty million. Her work has been translated into over thirty languages.<br /><br />In 2009 Brown detoured from romantic suspense to write, Rainwater, a much acclaimed, powerfully moving historical fiction story about honor and sacrifice during the Great Depression.<br /> <br />Brown was given an honorary Doctorate of Humane Letters from Texas Christian University. She was named Thriller Master for 2008, the top award given by the International Thriller Writer’s Association. Other awards and commendations include the 2007 Texas Medal of Arts Award for Literature and the Romance Writers of America’s Lifetime Achievement Award. <br /></span>
